+0000","feedId":13535,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"8c8d027ecc85a98ef4a26fa2cc3ba5b3","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"Sarah Dlin","publishedOrCreatedDate":1598323135044},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 10:38:55","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 10:38:55","title":"In Favor of Long, Image-light Ecommerce Emails","link":"https://copyhackers.com/?p=24496","description":"\n<p class=\"has-text-color has-small-font-size has-cyan-bluish-gray-color\">LAST UPDATED ON AUGUST 14, 2020</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We’ve written about email on Copyhackers… a lot.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And for good reason.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In 2019, email still has the highest ROI of any marketing channel ($42 return on every $1 spent, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://litmus.com/leadership/email-marketing-roi\" target=\"_blank\">according to Litmus</a>). And <a href=\"https://www.mckinsey.com/business-functions/marketing-and-sales/our-insights/why-marketers-should-keep-sending-you-emails\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">McKinsey</a> found that email is 40x more effective at acquiring customers than Facebook and Twitter &#8211; <em>combined.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Email just plain works.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And here at Copyhackers, we take optimizing email&#8230; seriously. Very seriously.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image2.gif?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25274\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\"/></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>We wrote about <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2017/06/free-trial-emails/\" target=\"_blank\">optimizing SaaS free trial emails</a>, <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2017/08/conversion-triggers-email-campaign/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">upgrading launch emails</a> and <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2017/09/cold-emails/\">sending B2B cold emails</a> that actually work.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Yet&#8230; we’ve never tackled this beast: <em>ecommerce</em></strong><strong> emails.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>But we’re not going to stay silent any longer.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>There’s too much at stake&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In ecommerce, the average order value from email is 20% higher with 3x the conversion rate <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://www.nerdmarketing.com/grow-profits-without-depending-on-google-facebook-ecommerce-email-strategies/\" target=\"_blank\">compared to other channels</a>. Email is your best fuel for <em>customer retention</em>, and <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://hbswk.hbs.edu/archive/the-economics-of-e-loyalty\" target=\"_blank\">Harvard Business School</a> found that just a 5% increase in retention can <em>increase profits by 95%.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Ecommerce emails done right can be the lifeblood of an ecommerce business.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Yet, many ecommerce stores are deeply underinvested in email.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Even though <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://myemma.s3.amazonaws.com/assets/files/content-download/emma-email-marketing-industry-report-2018.pdf\" target=\"_blank\">59% of marketers</a> say email gives the greatest ROI of any marketing channel&#8230; <a href=\"https://dma.org.uk/uploads/misc/589c5b9eaaca9-marketer-email-tracking-report-2017_589c5b9eaabde.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">64% of ecommerce marketers</a> expected their company’s email marketing budget to <em>increase or significantly increase</em> in the following year.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>They’re realizing they need to be spending more on email marketing.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Not surprising, given that Pure360 found in a survey of 205 marketers that <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://2ij7hk3p1vra3uhoox411gzf-wpengine.netdna-ssl.com/wp-content/uploads/2018/01/Pure360_Email_Maturity_Benchmarking_Report.pdf\" target=\"_blank\">9 out of 10 brands are behind the email marketing maturity standards they expected</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Beyond the numbers, it’s something that email consultants like myself see every day.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Austin Brawner, my friend and the CEO of <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://www.brandgrowthexperts.com/\" target=\"_blank\">Brand Growth Experts</a>, has had a similar experience to mine.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I once heard him say, “I’ve been in hundreds of email marketing accounts and I have yet to see someone who’s sending <em>too many</em> emails.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p>He’s right. Though many of us are worried about over-emailing, that’s rarely the problem. And big wins can come from small, strategic optimizations.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That’s why I almost always encourage clients to invest more in their email marketing. I know the impact it can have.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Like when I optimized the welcome sequence and abandoned cart sequence for my client, EcoVibe Style, I was able to increase their revenue from email to 38%&#8230; from a mere 8.7%.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That’s a 236% increase in revenue from email&#8230; <em>from just two sequences.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>But the difficulty isn’t in convincing store owners to care about email marketing. They know they <em>should </em>optimize their email marketing.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The struggle store owners are having&#8230; is in knowing <em>how</em> to go about optimizing their email marketing.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 class=\"has-text-align-center\">The (email marketing) struggle is real</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The <a href=\"https://dma.org.uk/uploads/misc/589c5b9eaaca9-marketer-email-tracking-report-2017_589c5b9eaabde.pdf\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">DMA’s email marketing survey</a> asked marketers about their most significant challenges to investing more in their email marketing.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Their top answers were: “limited internal resources,” “lack of strategy” and “lack of content.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So they want to send more emails&#8230; but they struggle to get the <strong>strategy and content expertise</strong> they need to do so.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Bottom line&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Ecommerce email marketing requires a great deal of expertise.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>There’s a lot of know-how that goes into emails that convert.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>There are sequences and newsletters, send times and from names, dozens of ESPs and email clients, subject lines and calls to action, exit intent pop-ups and floating bars&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When I started out as an email marketer, I was overwhelmed, too.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And when you finally decide on your strategy and get your technical pieces all set up, and it’s time to <em>write an actual email</em>… then you have to know what to put in that email.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You need to figure out what will get the attention of your recipients, so all that time and money you’ve invested actually pays off.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>When you finally sit down to write an email&#8230;</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>That’s the moment of truth.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Everything you’ve invested into your software and your content comes down to how well that email performs.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And… it’s only getting harder to win the inbox.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"https://expandedramblings.com/index.php/email-statistics/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">The typical professional receives an average of 121 emails per day.</a> Getting YOUR email to stand out is&#8230; <em>tough</em>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Marketers know how hard it’s getting.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Which is why some resort to a strategy I don’t recommend:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Sending sale email&#8230; after sale email… after sale email… after sale email&#8230;</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Every day, like clockwork, I get an email from Crate &#38; Barrel.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here, in my inbox, to announce a very exciting, ultra-exclusive, can-you-believe-it, hold-on-to-your-hat…. SALE SALE SALE!</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?resize=800%2C364&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25276\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?resize=800%2C364&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?resize=300%2C136&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?resize=150%2C68&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?resize=768%2C349&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?resize=1536%2C699&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?resize=990%2C450&#38;ssl=1 990w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?resize=1320%2C600&#38;ssl=1 1320w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image4-1.png?w=1926&#38;ssl=1 1926w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>And every day, their email goes… unopened.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But, I do understand <em>why</em> they send me these emails.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>It’s an easy pattern to fall into: you send an email blast and it doesn’t get the conversions you’re after. So you send another email with a steep 40% discount and &#8211; BAM! &#8211; lots of people buy.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You try to go back to sending an email <em>without a discount</em> but it’s still not working. So now you send…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>“FLASH SALE 70% OFF”</p>\n\n\n\n<p>&#8230;and you get lots of conversions again.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Before you know it, every email you send out is a sale email.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Even if you’re not quite at Crate &#38; Barrel’s level&#8230; it’s always tempting to send that sale email.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You want your email to pay off, after all. But&#8230; you also <em>don’t</em> want to get stuck sending emails that no one pays attention to.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And if you abuse the Sale Email, its magic starts to wear off.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The response from your subscribers changes from <em>buckets of revenue</em> to&#8230; <em>deafening silence.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Unlike <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2017/08/saas-onboarding-email/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">SaaS email marketing</a> &#8211; where the bias tends to be toward <em>nurturing</em> subscribers, rather than <em>selling</em> to them &#8211; it seems that ecommerce has the opposite trend: selling without nurturing.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And <a href=\"https://seths.blog/2008/01/permission-mark/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">Seth Godin would not approve</a>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The father of permission marketing, he revolutionized the way people think about marketing in the digital age:</p>\n\n\n\n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote\"><p><em>“Permission marketing is the privilege (not the right) of delivering anticipated, personal and relevant messages to people who actually want to get them. </em><strong><em>It recognizes the new power of the best consumers to ignore marketing.</em></strong><em>“ &#8211; Seth Godin</em></p></blockquote>\n\n\n\n<p>Marketing is easy to ignore. Especially in a crowded inbox.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So if you can send those <em>relevant, anticipated messages</em> your subscribers crave, you’ll be that unexpected gem people look forward to getting emails from.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And thinking of email as <em>permission-based marketing </em>sets us up well to answer the question&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 class=\"has-text-align-center\">Well, what <em>do</em> customers want <br>in their email marketing?</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>They want <em>variety.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>The problem with Crate &#38; Barrel’s emails isn’t that they’re sales emails.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>It’s that they’re ALL sales emails.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you’re having a sale tomorrow (and every day until the end of time), why should I be excited about today’s sale?</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If, however, every time you send me an email, I can’t be 100% sure what’s going to be in it (cool content? a funny story? new products? or maybe even a… SALE?!?), then I’m <em>anticipating</em> and wondering what’s in your email.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image26-1.gif?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25298\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\"/></figure>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Novelty is the best tool email marketers have to keep subscribers engaged.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><a href=\"http://help4teachers.com/ras.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">Neuroscience research</a> supports the idea that <em>novelty</em> is almost as effective at grabbing our attention as <em>physical need.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>&#8230;Meaning something <em>new</em> is almost as exciting to my brain as something that will satisfy my <em>hunger.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>(And I get <em>really</em> excited when I see a box of donuts.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You can also see proof of the <em>power of novelty</em> by looking at the counter-example…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>What happens when you don’t switch it up?</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I see this often with my clients: they’ll find a subject line that works well, so they reuse the same formula. But, pretty quickly… it stops working.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>It happened with one client recently&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>My client found great success with a subject line that followed the formula…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>“[Product] is back!”</p>\n\n\n\n<p>His email got an open rate <em>30% above</em> their average open rate.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Not too shabby.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>They used that same formula with a different product again, and this time they got another open rate <em>39.9% above average</em>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Great! This formula works like a charm.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But when they used it for a third time… their open rate unexpectedly dropped to 8.7% <em>below</em> their average open rate.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>What happened?</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>The subject line wasn’t <em>novel</em></strong><strong> anymore, so people stopped paying attention.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Very quickly&#8230; after just <em>three uses</em>&#8230; this subject line formula was dead.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>An <em>attention-grabbing air horn</em> can turn into <em>snooze-inducing white noise</em> pretty quickly in the world of email.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That’s why a combination of <em>sales emails</em> peppered in with <em>other kinds of emails</em> is your best chance to keep people interested.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 class=\"has-text-align-center\">Let’s see how top brands use novelty <br>in their email marketing</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Top brands that do this well use three different kinds of emails:</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>Sales emails</li><li>Nurture emails</li><li>Engagement emails</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<p>A sales email is going for the close &#8211; like a promotion or a product announcement.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>A nurture email is nurturing subscribers and building their affinity for the brand and product line.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And an engagement email is going for a click, rather than a sale &#8211; linking to content like blog posts, surveys and social media.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Kettle &#38; Fire, a brand selling <em>bone broth</em> to health-conscious customers, uses all three kinds of emails well.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>Sales emails</em> that provide discounts and make the case for their product:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image9.png?resize=800%2C858&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25281\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image9.png?resize=800%2C858&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image9.png?resize=280%2C300&#38;ssl=1 280w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image9.png?resize=140%2C150&#38;ssl=1 140w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image9.png?resize=768%2C823&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image9.png?resize=990%2C1061&#38;ssl=1 990w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image9.png?w=1196&#38;ssl=1 1196w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/3.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24534\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/3.png?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/3.png?resize=150%2C145&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/3.png?resize=300%2C290&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/3.png?resize=434%2C420&#38;ssl=1 434w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Sales email: abandoned cart.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Both emails are driving toward the use of a <em>coupon.</em> The welcome email is selling people on the brand, and the abandoned cart email is selling them on the product.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Kettle &#38; Fire is <em>anticipating</em> where the customer is at and, in turn, matching their message to what the customer needs to hear (i.e.: “You’re likely here because you heard bone broth promotes skin, nail, joint and digestive health.”)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>They also use <em>nurture emails</em> that educate people on bone broth and its importance for gut health:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/4.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24535\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/4.png?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/4.png?resize=150%2C132&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/4.png?resize=300%2C263&#38;ssl=1 300w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Nurture email.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This builds a loyal subscriber base that can point to reasons <em>why</em> Kettle &#38; Fire’s products are desirable.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And they send <em>engagement emails</em> that get people clicking through to their website and their content and building their relationship with Kettle &#38; Fire.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/5.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24536\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/5.png?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/5.png?resize=150%2C150&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/5.png?resize=300%2C300&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/5.png?resize=400%2C400&#38;ssl=1 400w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/5.png?resize=350%2C350&#38;ssl=1 350w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Engagement email.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>This email does a great job of showing why their content is worthy of a click &#8211; and sends readers clicking through to an email course.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Kettle &#38; Fire rotates between these three kinds of emails, always trying to anticipate where the customer is in their journey and giving them the message they need to hear at that moment.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Another brand that does this well is Moo, a company that sells business cards and stationery.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>They rely on design to drive curiosity in some <em>engagement emails:</em></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/6.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24537\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/6.png?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/6.png?resize=98%2C150&#38;ssl=1 98w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/6.png?resize=195%2C300&#38;ssl=1 195w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Moo engagement email.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/7.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24539\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/7.png?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/7.png?resize=102%2C150&#38;ssl=1 102w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/7.png?resize=204%2C300&#38;ssl=1 204w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Moo engagement email.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>And then go full plain-text in other <em>engagement emails:</em><br></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image15-2.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25287\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>And also send a mix of <em>sale</em> and <em>nurture emails:</em></p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/9.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24540\" https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/9.png?resize=224%2C300&#38;ssl=1 224w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 484px) 100vw, 484px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Moo sale email.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/10.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24541\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/10.png?w=541&#38;ssl=1 541w, 218w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 541px) 100vw, 541px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Moo nurture email.</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>A short sale email driving you to an exciting, unusual sale. And a welcome email nurturing you on the brand.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>These brands do it all. They use a variety of email types and use short emails alongside longer emails to engage their subscribers.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, I want to stop here, just in case the thought in the back of your head is&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 class=\"has-text-align-center\">“Wait, but people don’t read long emails. They want images, not text.”</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>If at this point, this is all making sense to you…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But you’re worried about sending longer emails that people have time to read…</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>There’s a study you might want to see.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>In 2014, <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/plain-text-vs-html-emails-data\" target=\"_blank\">Hubspot surveyed</a> thousands of people asking them what kind of email they preferred to receive: HTML or plain-text.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And their answers support the idea that you should send design-focused emails.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image22.png?resize=800%2C453&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25294\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image22.png?resize=800%2C453&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image22.png?resize=300%2C170&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image22.png?resize=150%2C85&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image22.png?resize=768%2C435&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image22.png?resize=990%2C560&#38;ssl=1 990w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image22.png?w=1258&#38;ssl=1 1258w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>They <em>said</em> they preferred HTML over plain-text.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And when HubSpot asked if they wanted mostly text or images in their emails, they said images.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image24-1.png?resize=800%2C576&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25296\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image24-1.png?resize=800%2C576&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image24-1.png?resize=300%2C216&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image24-1.png?resize=150%2C108&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image24-1.png?resize=768%2C553&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image24-1.png?resize=990%2C713&#38;ssl=1 990w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image24-1.png?w=1150&#38;ssl=1 1150w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>So… all of this would indicate that we should send short emails, right? More images. Less text. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Well, here’s where things get interesting…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>What people <em>say </em>they want in email vs. what emails they <em>actually</em> preferred to engage with… tell two completely different stories.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image1-2.png?resize=800%2C572&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25273\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image1-2.png?resize=800%2C572&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image1-2.png?resize=300%2C215&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image1-2.png?resize=150%2C107&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image1-2.png?resize=768%2C550&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image1-2.png?resize=990%2C708&#38;ssl=1 990w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image1-2.png?resize=1320%2C945&#38;ssl=1 1320w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image1-2.png?w=1350&#38;ssl=1 1350w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Increasing the design of HTML in the email &#8211; with more design and more images &#8211; actually <em>decreased</em> open rates. If you&#8217;re like &#8220;email content doesn&#8217;t affect open rates&#8221; (which it does), the study continues&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>HubSpot also found that emails with more images had <em>lower </em>click-through rates. Zero images in an email generated the highest click-through rates. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/14-1.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24549\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/14-1.png?w=700&#38;ssl=1 700w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/14-1.png?resize=150%2C122&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/14-1.png?resize=300%2C243&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/14-1.png?resize=260%2C210&#38;ssl=1 260w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>So it makes sense why many marketers believe that more images and more design is better for email marketing.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>After all, that’s what people <em>say </em>they want. But what creates actual <em>conversions</em> is text (ahem, copy!) and simple design.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But, there’s a place for both kinds of emails. Design-rich and text-rich emails nurture and engage subscribers in different ways. And you can use text-rich emails when you want to increase conversion rates. (I prefer the nice sound of a <em>ka-ching </em>to praise, personally.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So there’s a place for emails with more design than copy, and emails with more copy than design.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, we just need to figure out when a text-rich email makes sense and when you should be more to the point.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 class=\"has-text-align-center\">“How do I know <em>how long </em>to make my email? Then figure out&#8230; <em>what</em> to write in it??”</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Well, dear copyhacker…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s get copyhacking.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And let me show you the formula and template that will&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Let you determine exactly <em>how long</em></strong><strong> to make every ecommerce email you send. And solve the problem of <em>what copy</em></strong><strong> to include.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>We will do this by answering four questions:</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>What’s my One Reader’s <strong>beginning stage of awareness</strong>?</li><li>Where’s my One Reader in their <strong>customer lifecycle</strong>?</li><li><strong>How many emails</strong> are in this sequence?</li><li>What’s the <strong>one goal</strong> of my email?</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<p>(If you&#8217;re not sure about all this &#8220;One Reader&#8221; and &#8220;stage of awareness&#8221; talk, check out <a href=\"https://10xlandingpages.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\"10x Landing Pages by Copyhackers (opens in a new tab)\">10x Landing Pages by Copyhackers</a>. Yup, the foundational copywriting training in that course works for emails, too.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Cool! There’s your answer. End of article.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I kid, I kid.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s break down those four questions. And work through an example so it’s crystal clear.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>We can use the email sequence from the sustainable apparel client I referenced earlier. I’ll show you how I built their welcome sequence to get them their 236% increase in revenue from email.We’re going to answer the four questions, then use them to fill in <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\"this template (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://www.katiethies.co/ecommerce-email-template/\" target=\"_blank\"></a><a href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1bMn7GCMi7kA3Eox73R-HSuOsDzpN8ZCV4etyrRqijuk/copy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">this template</a> (which you can download for your own use):</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=800%2C199&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25279\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=800%2C199&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=300%2C75&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=150%2C37&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=768%2C191&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-button aligncenter is-style-default\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link has-background has-luminous-vivid-orange-background-color\" href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1bMn7GCMi7kA3Eox73R-HSuOsDzpN8ZCV4etyrRqijuk/copy\"><strong>Get this Template</strong>!<br><br></a></div>\n\n\n\n<p>And once that’s filled in, we’ll know <em>exactly</em> what content to include.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>(Don’t worry about that template for now. We’ll come back to it later.)</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Step 1. Find your One Reader’s beginning stage of awareness</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>If you’re not a seasoned copywriter yet, then stages of awareness may sound strange. Here’s a quick refresher:</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Picture a <em>slippery slope</em>.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>(Yes, I stole that from the <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://www.amazon.com/Adweek-Copywriting-Handbook-Advertising-Copywriters/dp/0470051248/ref=sr_1_3?crid=A1A9H7CD7PBQ&#38;keywords=the+adweek+copywriting+handbook&#38;qid=1566432074&#38;s=gateway&#38;sprefix=the+adweek+cop%2Caps%2C237&#38;sr=8-3\" target=\"_blank\">great Joe Sugarman</a>.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here&#8217;s <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2014/07/long-pages/\">h</a><a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2014/07/long-pages/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\"ow Joanna illustrates the stages of awareness and how they impact what you'll write (opens in a new tab)\">ow Joanna illustrates the stages of awareness and how they impact what you&#8217;ll write</a>:</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And here&#8217;s a modified view of that for ecommerce specifically:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?resize=800%2C372&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25282\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?resize=800%2C372&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?resize=300%2C139&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?resize=150%2C70&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?resize=768%2C357&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?resize=1536%2C714&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?resize=990%2C460&#38;ssl=1 990w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?resize=1320%2C614&#38;ssl=1 1320w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image10-1.png?w=1734&#38;ssl=1 1734w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>If your prospects (your not-yet customers) are sliding down a slippery slope, on their way to becoming your customers, then they need to move from pain aware all the way through most aware to get there.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>At each new stage, they come closer to buying your product, and importantly <strong>you cannot skip a stage.</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you want your prospect to turn into a customer, they cannot go from pain aware straight to most aware. They need solution awareness and product awareness to continue sliding down the slope.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So, in our example &#8211; the welcome sequence for the sustainable apparel brand &#8211; our one reader is new to our brand and probably knows little about what we offer.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So, in this case, I assumed they were in the earliest stage of awareness: pain aware. We use that information to answer the first question:</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>What’s my One Reader’s <strong>beginning stage of awareness</strong>?<br>Pain aware.</li><li>Where’s my One Reader in their <strong>customer lifecycle?</strong></li><li><strong>How many emails are in this sequence?</strong></li><li><strong>What’s the one goal</strong> of my email?</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<p>Great. One down, three to go.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Step 2. Figure out where your One Reader is in their customer lifecycle</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Lifecycle marketing is the idea that customers go through a… well, lifecycle.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In the early stages, a prospect becomes aware of you. Then they buy from you. (Hooray!) Then, they might buy from you again. (Whoopee!)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>&#8230;But eventually they lose interest in your products or stop needing them (how many {something funny} does one woman need anyway?) and they move on.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>A sad day, but an inevitable one.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>To visualize, the customer lifecycle looks like:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?resize=800%2C271&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25295\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?resize=800%2C271&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?resize=300%2C102&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?resize=150%2C51&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?resize=768%2C261&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?resize=1536%2C521&#38;ssl=1 1536w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?resize=990%2C336&#38;ssl=1 990w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?resize=1320%2C448&#38;ssl=1 1320w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image23-1.png?w=1760&#38;ssl=1 1760w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Here are the main stages to remember, as they relate to email marketing:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li><strong>New:</strong> New to our brand, never purchased</li><li><strong>Abandoned cart:</strong> Close to purchasing</li><li><strong>Post-purchase:</strong> Just after purchasing from the brand</li><li><strong>Lifecycle:</strong> The natural lifecycle of a product when it would make sense to purchase again (e.g. for a 30-day supply of vitamins, the lifecycle would be 30 days)</li><li><strong>Winback:</strong> When a customer has lapsed and is not purchasing at the normal lifecycle interval.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>For our example…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Since it’s a <em>welcome sequence</em>, then we’re sending these to prospects who are new. They have yet to make a purchase from us.</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>What’s my One Reader’s <strong>beginning stage of awareness</strong>?<br>Pain aware.</li><li>Where’s my One Reader in their <strong>customer lifecycle</strong>?<br>New</li><li><strong>How many emails</strong> are in this sequence?</li><li>What’s the <strong>one goal</strong> of my email?</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<p>Moving right along&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Step 3. How many emails are in your sequence?</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, this is something you can decide before you start creating content for your email sequence. It depends on the timing of your emails and how long you want your sequence to run.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you’re sending a newsletter, then that would be a one-off and you can just fill in &#8216;one&#8217;. (The formula works the same way for newsletters.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>To help you decide how many emails to include in your sequence, <a href=\"https://www.klaviyo.com/blog/triggered-emails-ecommerce\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">here’s benchmark data from Klaviyo</a> on how emails perform based on how many there are in the sequence:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image12-1.png?resize=800%2C721&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25284\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image12-1.png?resize=800%2C721&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image12-1.png?resize=300%2C270&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image12-1.png?resize=150%2C135&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image12-1.png?resize=768%2C692&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image12-1.png?resize=990%2C892&#38;ssl=1 990w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image12-1.png?w=1192&#38;ssl=1 1192w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>For my sequence, I wanted to send four emails (so I could send a mix of sales and nurture emails). So let’s answer question #3.</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>What’s my One Reader’s <strong>beginning stage of awareness</strong>?<br>Pain aware.</li><li>Where’s my One Reader in their <strong>customer lifecycle</strong>?<br>New</li><li><strong>How many emails</strong> are in this sequence?<br>4</li><li>What’s the <strong>one goal</strong> of my email?</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<h3>Step 4. Figure out the goal of your email</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>And finally, we move from questions about the entire sequence to questions about each individual email.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>To do this, we need to refer back to our template from earlier:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=800%2C199&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25279\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=800%2C199&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=300%2C75&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=150%2C37&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=768%2C191&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, let’s fill in the pieces that we already answered from the first three questions: lifecycle, stage of awareness and number of emails.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image11-1.png?resize=800%2C316&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25283\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image11-1.png?resize=800%2C316&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image11-1.png?resize=300%2C118&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image11-1.png?resize=150%2C59&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image11-1.png?resize=768%2C303&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image11-1.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, for each of the four emails in this sequence, we need to decide on what <em>kind</em> of email we’re going to send: nurture, sales or engage.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Determine the kind of email you’ll send based on your goal:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>Sales emails <em>sell</em>, so their KPI is revenue (if you&#8217;re generating more orders) or average order value (if you&#8217;re generating larger orders).</li><li>Nurture emails <em>nurture</em>, so the KPI&#8230; depends.</li><li>Engagement emails <em>engage</em>, so their KPIs are click-through rate followed by active time on site.</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, let’s look at my welcome sequence for my sustainable apparel client.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In my four-email welcome sequence, I’m going to send:</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>A welcome email with a discount coupon (which is the incentive to opt-in).</li><li>A nurture email that tells a story about the brand.</li><li>A second nurture email that tells another story about the brand.</li><li>A reminder email &#8211; that their discount coupon (from email #1) is expiring today.</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<p>That means emails #1, #2 and #3 are nurture emails because we’re nurturing new subscribers. And email #4 is a sales email because it’s the final email in the sequence and it’s closing on the expiring discount. So now our template looks like this:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image8-1.png?resize=800%2C313&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25280\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image8-1.png?resize=800%2C313&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image8-1.png?resize=300%2C117&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image8-1.png?resize=150%2C59&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image8-1.png?resize=768%2C301&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image8-1.png?w=874&#38;ssl=1 874w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>(Note: email #1 has <em>Sales</em> listed as a secondary goal. We won’t use that in our formula, but I included it because we may want to use revenue as a KPI for that email &#8211; since it has a discount coupon included.)</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Now, let’s use our formula to fill in all the grey cells for us.</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Here’s the formula that will eliminate the guesswork from how long to make our emails:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>For nurture emails</strong>, the ending stage of awareness of that email is one stage past the beginning stage of awareness of that email (e.g. Problem → Solution, Solution → Product).</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>For sales emails</strong>, it doesn’t matter what the beginning stage of awareness is. The ending stage of awareness is always <em>most aware.</em> (Since we’re trying to make the sale).</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>For engagement emails</strong>, the beginning and ending stages of awareness are the same. Since we’re trying to engage, not sell.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>To make it easy, here’s your handy-dandy formula:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Nurture email: Add +1 to Stage of Awareness</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Sales email: Ending SoA = Most Aware</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Engagement email: Beginning SoA = Ending SoA</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>So for our example welcome sequence, this fills in the rest of our template to look like this:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image17-1.png?resize=800%2C372&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25289\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image17-1.png?resize=800%2C372&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image17-1.png?resize=300%2C139&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image17-1.png?resize=150%2C70&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image17-1.png?resize=768%2C357&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image17-1.png?w=878&#38;ssl=1 878w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Of course, this formula didn’t give me the description of our One Reader at the top.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I got that from all my voice of customer research. (You can check out content from master researchers &#8211; like <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/how-to-master-customer-interviews/\">the tutorial of Copyhackers&#8217;s own Hannah Shamji on getting quality VoC from customer interviews</a> &#8211; to learn how to get inside the head of your One Reader.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Armed with your VoC research, and now with this template, you can see how to work your VoC data into the email sequence you’re building.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, I made two promises to you…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That you’d know <em>how long</em> to make your emails AND that it would become clear <em>what</em> to write in your emails.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So let’s see how this template helps us with both of these problems.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Problem #1: Knowing <em>how</em> <em>long </em>to make your email</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Just as the original conversion copywriter, Joanna Wiebe, teaches: copy is as long as it <em>needs to be.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>And you can figure out how long a piece of copy needs to be&#8230; by looking at the beginning and ending stages of awareness.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>(Where your prospect is now vs. where they need to be for your goal.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This template shows our beginning and ending stages of awareness <em>for each email.</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s look at emails #1 and #4 from our sequence to see how this template influenced their length.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you remember, both emails are giving a discount to the subscriber. So it would seem like they’d be identical in length. Right?</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But what the template shows us, is:</p>\n\n\n\n<ul><li>Email #1 moves from problem aware to solution aware</li><li>Email #4 is already at most aware &#8211; and stays there</li></ul>\n\n\n\n<p>So email #1 is <em>slightly longer</em> than email #4 because it has more work to do. And email #4 is just going for the close. </p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/18.png?resize=427%2C1024&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24543\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/18.png?resize=427%2C1024&#38;ssl=1 427w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/18.png?resize=63%2C150&#38;ssl=1 63w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/18.png?resize=125%2C300&#38;ssl=1 125w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/18.png?w=500&#38;ssl=1 500w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 427px) 100vw, 427px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Email #1</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/19.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24544\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/19.png?w=700&#38;ssl=1 700w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/19.png?resize=110%2C150&#38;ssl=1 110w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/19.png?resize=220%2C300&#38;ssl=1 220w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /><figcaption>Email #4</figcaption></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>They’re both <em>discount, promotional emails</em>, but that’s not what determines length. It’s the stages of awareness from our template that we need to adhere to. <strong>Here&#8217;s how to figure out how long your email should be:</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>The greater the distance between our beginning and ending stage of awareness of the email (with problem to most aware being the greatest), the longer our email needs to be.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So, length: solved.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Problem #2: Knowing <em>what</em> to write in your email</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, this is the real magic of filling out the entire template.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>To find <em>what </em>content is best, you need only to isolate the email that you’re currently writing and find the copy that solves your problem.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s look at email #2 for this one.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image14-1.png?resize=800%2C377&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25286\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image14-1.png?resize=800%2C377&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image14-1.png?resize=300%2C141&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image14-1.png?resize=150%2C71&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image14-1.png?resize=768%2C362&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image14-1.png?w=874&#38;ssl=1 874w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>For this email, we’re moving the One Reader from solution to product aware for sustainable apparel.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So she knows about other sustainable apparel options, but she wants to know why our line of clothing in particular is better than our competitors&#8217;. <em>And</em> she’s frustrated that most sustainable clothes don’t look great and are expensive.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Bingo.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Now, all I have to do is weave the VoC I have from my research into an email about how problems with sustainable clothing shopping (the solution) are solved by a particular brand: EcoVibe (the product).</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And the resulting email…</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/20.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24545\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/20.png?w=333&#38;ssl=1 333w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/20.png?resize=97%2C150&#38;ssl=1 97w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/20.png?resize=194%2C300&#38;ssl=1 194w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 333px) 100vw, 333px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Armed with this template, and your voice-of-customer data, writing your email is largely done before you even open up your blank Google Doc. You know where to start, which is a great way to end Blank Page Syndrome. And you know your destination, which means you&#8217;re less likely to ramble. Now just plug that VoC into a <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2015/10/copywriting-formula/\">compelling framework</a>! Well, there&#8217;s a little more to it&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 class=\"has-text-align-center\">“I still don’t want to send long emails.”</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>If you’re still against writing a longer email with more than just a sentence or two of copy…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Darling, let’s not fight.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s compromise.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>Try</em> writing an email with just a bit more length, but feel confident by putting a call-to-action above the fold.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Like I did in the first email of this sequence:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/21.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24546\" srcset=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/21.png?w=450&#38;ssl=1 450w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/21.png?resize=112%2C150&#38;ssl=1 112w, https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/21.png?resize=224%2C300&#38;ssl=1 224w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 450px) 100vw, 450px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>So no one has to read, if they don’t want to. They can click-through right away.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>(And you and I can pick up this discussion later.)</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 class=\"has-text-align-center\">“Okay, but what about campaign emails? Those go to a variety of people.”</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>You are absolutely right. I’ve got a suggestion for how to handle the varied audience of a typical email newsletter, but first I want to say&#8230;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>THIS is exactly why segmentation is so powerful.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Segmentation helps you know which portion of your audience you’re speaking to, where they are in their customer lifecycle and what their stage of awareness is. The better your segmentation, the more you can dial-in your messaging and use this formula to your advantage. (Jo talks more about segmentation inside 10x Emails.)</p>\n\n\n\n<p>But if you (like many ecommerce stores) are sending newsletters to your whole list…</p>\n\n\n\n<p>You should switch it up between longer and shorter emails. Just like the examples I showed you above from Kettle &#38; Fire. By getting different messages to your email list, you’ll get more of the right message to more of the right people.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Use <em>nurture</em>, <em>sales</em> and <em>engagement</em> emails to engage your whole email list. Use variety to target the natural segments within your email list.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>A quick note on the <em>engagement</em> email &#8211;<br>the bread-and-butter of email newsletters.</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Many times your campaign emails will be <em>engagement </em>emails. That’s the classic newsletter email that people think of when they think of marketing emails, where you link to content and try to get people to click through.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So let’s talk about what an <em>engagement</em> email should look like. Since, from our formula, you remember that the beginning and ending stages of awareness are the same.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Engagement emails, as you expect, should be very short.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Our stage of awareness doesn’t change with an engagement email. The content that people click through to might change their stage of awareness, but that’s not <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2015/03/measure-your-copy-infographic/\">our email’s job</a>. Our email’s job is to get them to that content.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So, here, the copy should be very short. Just enough to entice them to want to know what’s after that button.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That’s why the very short Moo engagement email works.</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/7-1.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24547\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/7-1.png?w=600&#38;ssl=1 600w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/7-1.png?resize=102%2C150&#38;ssl=1 102w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/7-1.png?resize=204%2C300&#38;ssl=1 204w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 600px) 100vw, 600px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>It’s doing just enough to get you curious, and not distracting you with anything else.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Copyhackers also sends engagement emails that follow this principle:</p>\n\n\n\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter\"><img src=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/22.png?ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-24548\" srcset=\"https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/22.png?w=624&#38;ssl=1 624w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/22.png?resize=102%2C150&#38;ssl=1 102w, https://i1.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/09/22.png?resize=204%2C300&#38;ssl=1 204w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 624px) 100vw, 624px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure></div>\n\n\n\n<p>Just enough to make your curious about the content. Nothing else to distract.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>It’s your sales emails and nurture emails that will be longer. Since those need to bring your subscribers further along in their journey. So make sure you’re still including engagement emails in your email newsletter strategy.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2 class=\"has-text-align-center\">Your ecommerce emails&#8230; <br>mapped, wrapped and ready </h2>\n\n\n\n<p>By answering the following four questions:</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>What’s my One Reader’s <strong>beginning stage of awareness</strong>?</li><li>Where’s my One Reader in their <strong>customer lifecycle</strong>?</li><li><strong>How many emails</strong> are in this sequence?</li><li>What’s the <strong>one goal</strong> of my email?</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<p>And armed with our voice of customer data and the answers to those four questions, we are able to fill in the white cells of this chart:</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=800%2C199&#038;ssl=1\" alt=\"\" class=\"wp-image-25279\" srcset=\"https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=800%2C199&#38;ssl=1 800w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=300%2C75&#38;ssl=1 300w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=150%2C37&#38;ssl=1 150w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?resize=768%2C191&#38;ssl=1 768w, https://i0.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/04/image7-1.png?w=876&#38;ssl=1 876w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 800px) 100vw, 800px\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\" /></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>Then, use the following formula to automatically fill in the remaining grey cells:</p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Nurture email: Add +1 to Stage of Awareness</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Sales email: Ending SoA = Most Aware</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p><strong>Engagement email: Beginning SoA = Ending SoA</strong></p>\n\n\n\n<p>We’ve mapped out the entire content strategy of any ecommerce email sequence.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Whether the emails you’re sending are automated, a single newsletter, a 10-email long sequence… or any other hypothetical you can imagine, with these tools in your arsenal, your email content strategy is solved.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>So you never have to stare at 10:38:55","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 10:38:55","title":"3 Customer Interview Techniques to Get Rich Customer Data","link":"https://copyhackers.com/?p=24690","description":"\n<p><em>When customer interviews go badly, with one-word answers or poor engagement, try these three things: vocalize pauses, repeat back responses and &#8220;name their claim.&#8221; </em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>One question into your interview, the worst is clear: </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Your customer is <em>not</em> a talker.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Managing the customer interview and drawing out valuable customer data is, of course, your job. But landing a one-word answer when you’re anticipating a meaty response is an unpleasant surprise &#8211; no matter how good an interviewer you are.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And if you’re not braced to handle such unpleasantries, you&#8217;ll be thrown off-kilter and off-script.</p>\n\n\n\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\"><img src=\"https://i2.wp.com/copyhackers.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/11/customer-interviews.gif?ssl=1\" alt=\"Don't let an awkward customer interview throw you off-kilter!\" class=\"wp-image-24693\" data-recalc-dims=\"1\"/></figure>\n\n\n\n<p>So before you hop on your next customer interview call, prep yourself with these three psychology-backed strategies to move beyond the awkward silence and glean rich nuggets of insight, even when your customer dishes out the tiniest of sentence fragments.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Technique 1: Bring the customer interview to a momentary halt with a vocal pause&#160;</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>Yes, it’s your job to keep the conversation going. But more important than continuity is keeping the conversation on track.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The<em> right track.</em>&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>The track where you end that Zoom recording with a deep and intimate understanding of who your customer truly is &#8211; and with <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\" href=\"https://copyhackers.com/how-to-use-voc-to-create-outlines-with-hannah-shamji/\" target=\"_blank\">voice-of-customer data you can actually swipe</a>.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here’s how:&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>When your customer answers short, you go long &#8211; and take what I call a “vocal pause”&#160;</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>A vocal pause is when you intentionally hesitate a second to regroup after being caught off guard, but you say something over the silence to mask it. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Examples of a vocal pause include: </p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>“Hmm, that’s interesting, okay.”</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>“I see, I see.”</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>“Okay, okay, that makes sense.”</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>“Ah, okay. Hmm, so let me see….”</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p>These are filler words. They mean little, but they accomplish a lot: they help you take pause without actually pausing.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This<img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f44f.png\" alt=\"👏\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /> is<img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f44f.png\" alt=\"👏\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" />key <img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f44f.png\" alt=\"👏\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" />, folks.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>If you don’t pause and instead panic and hop over to the next question, you’re wasting a golden opportunity to dig deeper.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>It’s okay to be caught off guard. It happens. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>And with the vocal pause, you can still save face and stay in the driver’s seat of your customer interview &#8211; before you reroute to a sharper question.</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Technique 2: Double-check your customer’s response&#160;</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>This step’s a tad cheeky, but it works.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you’ve had a sec to recalibrate (a la Technique 1), the easiest and smartest way to dive back into the interview is to double-check where your customer is at.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>How?</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Say what you heard them say right back at &#8217;em. In their words. Then, cheekily check you’ve got it right.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>I’ll show you what that sounds like in a minute, but here’s why it works. It’s called active listening, and done right, it achieves two monumental goals:</p>\n\n\n\n<ol><li><strong>It tells your customer <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/2018/05/how-to-listen/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">you’re actually listening</a>!</strong> Which is huge. And ridiculously uncommon. When people feel <em>that</em> heard, they can’t help but feel THIIIIIIIIIIS AMOUNT of safe. And feeling safe is directly tied to how willing they are to open up to you… a stranger.&#160;&#160;</li><li><strong>When you reflect back what you heard your customer say, you’re kickstarting a sentence &#8211; </strong><em><strong>their</strong></em><strong> </strong><em><strong>sentence</strong></em><strong> &#8211; for them to finish.</strong> Which they will. And nine times out of 10, they’ll add a little extra.&#160;</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<p>This is how you start to dig deep &#8211; by turning your customer interview into a conversation.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Here’s an example of a customer interview, which I like to use when I lead customer research workshops:&#160;</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>The interviewer below was trying to unpack why the customer chose a particular brand of cat food, but the customer kept coming back with an unhelpful response: “Well, I just go to the shop and buy it.”&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>In a role play, I used the double-check technique to dig deeper. Take a look at what happened.</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer:</strong> “I just go into the store and get it. It’s what’s on the shelf.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f482-200d-2640-fe0f.png\" alt=\"💂‍♀️\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Interviewer:</strong> “I see. Okay. So you buy that cat food because it’s just what’s in the store, what’s on the shelf. Did I get that right, or… ?”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer:</strong> “Yeah, it’s just there. It’s convenient and it’s the one I know.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Bingo! Now we’re onto something.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Thanks to a super simple double-check, we now know that the customer is deeply loyal to his brand. So loyal he doesn’t think twice about it. To know it’s not just a matter of convenience and apathy like we thought at first, is actually a pretty big deal (<a href=\"https://www.destinationcrm.com/Articles/Web-Exclusives/Viewpoints/The-Psychology-of-Loyalty-100641.aspx\">see why</a>).&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>Let’s break down how we got to that insight using this customer interviewing technique:</h3>\n\n\n\n<ol><li>First, the customer offered up a two-dimensional answer. Nothing rich or emotional.&#160;</li><li>I paused, repeated it back to him IN HIS WORDS, and&#8230;</li><li>Checked if I’d gotten it right.&#160;How did I double-check? Here’s the clincher. By adding a two-letter word at the end of my question: “or?”. This mighty word flipped my double-check from a closed to an open-ended question.</li><li>And that’s exactly what helped the customer, all on his own, to take a step further and share more detail.</li></ol>\n\n\n\n<p>See, most people don’t have well-thought out reasons for why they buy the things they do. They need your help to tease it out.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you repeat back what they <em>are</em> telling you, they get a chance to a) hear it and b) correct it.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>This helps you both unpack their true, unconscious rationale &#8211; together.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Technique 3: &#8220;Name their claim</strong>&#8220;</h2>\n\n\n\n<p>What if you do a vocal pause, double-check what you heard and your customer still dishes out a plain old “Yes, that’s right” when you reflect back?&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Are you doomed? Is my three-step technique a farce?</p>\n\n\n\n<p>No and no.</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Here’s the game plan.</p>\n\n\n\n<h3>If your customer still isn’t giving you much and you want to go even deeper, here’s how:&#160;</h3>\n\n\n\n<p>Give what your customer just shared a name. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Call it something. </p>\n\n\n\n<p>Is it convenience? Is it ease? Is it a no-brainer? Is it being cost effective?&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>See, even though people have lived their own experience and know it by heart, most haven’t had to talk about it. Which means they don’t know how to describe or articulate it. To do that, your customer needs your help.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>And this is really good news for you.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you strap words to your customer’s personal experience, it’s like adding color to a black and white image. It’s a welcome attention to detail.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>That, and naming their claim also gives them something to react to.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>They can yay or nay the label you&#8217;ve offered, and help you finetune and flesh it out.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Let’s see it in action. We’ll use the same interview as above so you get a fuller picture.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer:</strong><em> </em>“I just go into the store and get it. It’s what’s on the shelf.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f482-200d-2640-fe0f.png\" alt=\"💂‍♀️\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Interviewer:</strong> “I see. Okay. [VOCAL PAUSE] So you buy that cat food because it’s just what’s in the store, what’s on the shelf. Did I get that right, or… ?” [DOUBLE-CHECK]&nbsp;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer:</strong> “Yeah, it’s just there. It’s convenient and it’s the one I know.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f482-200d-2640-fe0f.png\" alt=\"💂‍♀️\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Interviewer:</strong> “Ah, okay. So you pick it because you know… that it’s good? [NAMING] That it’s worked before so it’ll work again?” [NAMING]&nbsp;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer:</strong> “Yeah, yeah.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f482-200d-2640-fe0f.png\" alt=\"💂‍♀️\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Interviewer:</strong> “Okay, makes sense. [VOCAL PAUSE] Is that a convenience thing?” [NAMING]\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer: </strong>“Yeah, yeah.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><em>At this point, I have enough of the story to start unpacking it, which is exactly what I proceed to do&#8230;</em></p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f482-200d-2640-fe0f.png\" alt=\"💂‍♀️\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Interviewer:</strong> “Okay, so, let me ask you this. Are there other cat food options at the store?”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer:</strong> “Don’t know, I just picked that one.”&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f482-200d-2640-fe0f.png\" alt=\"💂‍♀️\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Interviewer:</strong> “So you don&#8217;t really pay attention to what other ones there are?”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer:</strong> “No, I just get the same one every time.”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f482-200d-2640-fe0f.png\" alt=\"💂‍♀️\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Interviewer:</strong> “It sounds like getting the same one is maybe easier. Like you don&#8217;t have to think about it. You just trust that brand? Is that right?”</p>\n\n\n\n<p><img src=\"https://s.w.org/images/core/emoji/12.0.0-1/72x72/1f468.png\" alt=\"👨\" class=\"wp-smiley\" style=\"height: 1em; max-height: 1em;\" /><strong>Customer: </strong>“Yeah, yeah. I like that brand, it works for me, why change what’s working.”&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<h2><strong>Do you see the pattern here?</strong></h2>\n\n\n\n<p>The job of the interviewer isn’t just to administer a reel of pre-determined <a href=\"https://www.producttalk.org/2016/03/customer-interview-questions/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">customer interview questions</a>. It’s to dive right in with the customer and unpack their story with them.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>When you’re with a tight-lipped customer, they’re not skirting you out of spite or because they’re consciously holding out.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>They genuinely don’t have more to say, and often, it’s because they haven’t thought it through. They haven’t looked into why they bought this brand at that store.&#160;</p>\n\n\n\n<p>Understanding that <a href=\"https://copyhackers.com/how-to-master-customer-interviews/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" aria-label=\" (opens in a new tab)\">mastering your job as customer interviewer</a> means helping your customer realize what you want to know &#8211; that’s the difference between a dud of an interview packed with one-word dead ends and an interview so insightful, you can’t take notes fast enough. </p>\n<script type=\"text/javascript\">\n\nwindow.rmpanda =
